--- Commit Message ---
LU-12682 llite: fake symlink type of foreign file/dir

This patch implements a "fake symlink" specific usage of
"foreign" LOV/LMV format. It basically allows these
particular type of foreign files/dirs to behave as a
symlink from VFS point of view, by allowing to construct
a relative path from the LOV/LMV foreign content, to
complement it with a prefix, and then to expose it to
the VFS as a symlink destination. The default/internal
mechanism simply takes the full foreign free string as
the relative path, and for more complex internal formats
an upcall has been implemented to provide format's
details (presently just in terms of constant strings
and substrings positions in EA, but this can be enhanced)
to llite layer.
Using this feature, instead of real symlinks or user EA,
will permit to benefit from the special features (lock,
prefetch, caches) already implemented to handle both
LOV/LMV EAs.

Signed-off-by: Bruno Faccini <bruno.faccini@intel.com>

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2019-11-24 20:56:41.000000000) ---
Patch Set 13:

(36 comments)

I'm really not a fan of having DAOS-specific layout interpreting inside the kernel. Can this be more generic?  It should be enough to just check the foreign layout type?

It seems like the bulk of this code is just parsing the DAOS foreign layout and interpreting it as a slightly-different symlink. Why not just return the actual xattr string as the symlink target and deal with this in userspace?

I'm not against the idea of interpreting foreign layouts as symlinks, but it shouldn't be necessary to parse them in the kernel.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2019-12-04 00:47:09.000000000) ---
Patch Set 18:

Bruno, I haven't had a chance to look at the latest patch, but regarding userland parsing/generation of the symlinks - I was thinking that since DAOS is using FUSE and/or other IO forwarding in front of the filesystem for the clients that it would make sense to generate the DAOS symlink in the dfuse driver?

For non-FUSE clients, I don't think the symlink is useful anyways?  Maybe I'm wrong about how you are going to use this, in which case it would be good to have some better idea of how it is going to be used.

--- Message (Bruno Faccini, 2019-12-04 17:43:53.000000000) ---
Patch Set 18:

Hello Andreas, I was a bit surprised by your answer, but talking with Johann it may come from the fact you refer to the old DAOS Client node design where IOF/Fuse was always present as the front-end, but with the new design this is Lustre Client that is used as the front-end and this is what justifies for the main changes in this patch. May be we can discuss/detail all of this off-line if you want ?? You may also now better understand my own question/comment concerning how you think the user-land parsing should be implemented ? May be by passing EA content to some user-land upcall (registered for DAOS type) to do the parsing ? But since it should allow for multiple requests to run in parallel, may be you could point me to some already existing piece of similar code in Lustre ?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2019-12-10 04:52:24.000000000) ---
Patch Set 19:

(11 comments)

> Hello Andreas, I was a bit surprised by your answer, but talking
 > with Johann it may come from the fact you refer to the old DAOS
 > Client node design where IOF/Fuse was always present as the
 > front-end, but with the new design this is Lustre Client that is
 > used as the front-end and this is what justifies for the main
 > changes in this patch.

You are right that I thought DAOS had its own userspace component that could interpret this.

 > You may also now better understand my own
 > question/comment concerning how you think the user-land parsing
 > should be implemented ? May be by passing EA content to some
 > user-land upcall (registered for DAOS type) to do the parsing ? But
 > since it should allow for multiple requests to run in parallel, may
 > be you could point me to some already existing piece of similar
 > code in Lustre ?

Definitely this patch is adding a lot of "policy" to the kernel, which would be very difficult to get into the upstream client.  Having an upcall to do the symlink lookup would be much more flexible.

A similar functionality exists in the l_getidentity upcall to map a UID to a list of supplemental GIDs.  This would take the binary DAOS layout (including the magic), pass it to userspace, and userspace would return the symlink target.  That allows it to be totally flexible in changing the mountpoints for the DAOS containers (e.g. depending on the site configuration) rather than having to patch Lustre to handle changes.  Doing a pure upcall would be the most flexible for sure.  If you don't expect a large number of such symlinks to be accessed and performance is not critical.

Another option would be to have a DAOS upcall that is called only rarely for a filesystem and returns a format string that allows printing out the symlink directly in the kernel, for example "/mnt/daos/myds/%pUb/%pUb" or similar (see linux/Documentation/core-api/printk-formats.rst in the kernel sources).  There would also need to be some way to specify how the binary field offsets are mapped to the arguments.

Finally another option would be to have the llite code request a module like "llite-foreign-<type>" that has very simple functions to generate the symlink from the layout and isolate it from the core Lustre code.

I think the easiest option would be to start by moving the foreign symlink code into a separate llite-foreign.c file, would at least be a good start, and avoid sprinkling the foreign layout code around llite.

--- Message (Ben Evans, 2020-02-27 21:38:07.000000000) ---
Patch Set 25: Code-Review+1

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-02-27 22:37:13.000000000) ---
Patch Set 25:

> (1 comment)
 > 
 > Note the LL_IOC_REMOVE_ENTRY was really disliked by Al Viro for
 > security reasons. In fact it was removed upstream. I see something
 > similar here.

I can understand that Al didn't like this, but it is also something that we need to have in some form or another.  This is something that can't really happen in a local filesystem - that a name exists in a directory that doesn't have a real inode associated with it, or that cannot be opened.

I could imagine some other way of handling this, maybe with an ioctl on a file/dir opened by O_PATH, but that could be done independently of this patch, since we still have/need "lfs rmentry" in the out-of-tree Lustre, even if it isn't going into the upstream client.

(4 comments)

Currently, this defaults to 'foreign file/dir cannot be removed without calling ioctl first'.  So, "prevent remove" (or whatever) is on by default.  Is that the default we want?  Or should we make that a special thing that can be set when creating the file?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-09-01 17:59:58.000000000) ---
Patch Set 40:

(4 comments)

Patrick,
I think there *is* an upcall included in this patch - lustre/utils/l_foreign_symlink.c but the problem you describe about having to register multiple upcalls does still exist.

I found my previous review comment from 2020-02-04:

 > If there are multiple different foreign types, it would be useful
 > to run the upcall as "l_foreign_symlink-%x" or something, where
 > "%x" is the hex type of the foreign layout.  That allows multiple
 > upcalls to co-exist for different layout types, rather than this
 > binary having to understand every possible foreign type at the
 > same time.

And thanks for reviewing this patch again.  Unfortunately, there seem to be widely differing opinions on whether parts of the patch are acceptable, which are preventing forward progress toward landing.  

Maybe in your review you can see some way to address the various issues.  In particular the need for blocking regular "unlink" of foreign files and needing a special interface seems to be contentious, but I haven't been keeping up with all the details.

One option might be something like an "immutable" flag (LMAC_IMMUTABLE?) that can be set/cleared by regular users instead of the current IMMUTABLE flag that can only be set/cleared by root.  That is not a bigger barrier than running "lfs foreign_unlink" to delete such a file accidentally, but at least provides a first-level defense against accidental removal of the file and then when it is cleared normal "rm" would work?  That would also be useful for other purposes beyond foreign layouts that have come up in the past.

--- Message (Patrick Farrell (personal), 2020-09-01 18:27:55.000000000) ---
Patch Set 40: -Code-Review

Andreas,

Hm, you're right about the presence of that upcall.  I can't see where it gets enabled, but it does seem to be used in the tests.

I like your suggestion for multiple types of foreign layout.  Something like that seems essential - It's easy to imagine a future system that has, eg, DAOS, and some HSM-like slower tier on the same machine.

My thoughts on blocking unlink:
1. I think your suggestion of making it available to all Lustre files and users is an excellent one.
2. We could still have lfs/llapi_foreign_unlink command/api CALL, it could just be something that automatically unset the special immutable flag.

This also makes it a bit more "opt-in".  The API for creating fake symlinks can set it on by default (but also make it a choice for the caller).

About the flag, for a name, perhaps unremovable, as immutable has another meaning, unless you *want* those semantics...?  I guess it wouldn't be hard to add true immutable, but it's implemented outside of Lustre today.  It would basically have to go at every entry point for write or setattr/setxattr.

--- Message (Bruno Faccini, 2020-09-07 15:02:55.000000000) ---
Patch Set 40:

(8 comments)

Concerning the unlink/rm of foreign symlink file/dir, it is already being done by setting the LLIF_FOREIGN_REMOVABLE inode flag using ioctl(fd, LL_IOC_UNLOCK_FOREIGN), which has the effect to make the following unlink to be successful. And again IMMUTABLE flag usage has been investigated during this same patch development, but was far too restrictive.

I will try to implement the per-type user-upcall capability you are requesting, along with all the answers/fixes to your others comments, but I will do that in an add-on patch to be added on top of this patch, this to prevent any divergence with master-next branch where this patch is now waiting since several weeks now.

--- Message (Patrick Farrell (personal), 2020-09-08 17:43:30.000000000) ---
Patch Set 40:

Bruno,

OK, that sounds good to do another patch on top of this.

One remaining thought.

Andreas, Bruno,

Question for you - How do you feel about still having the unremovable flag limited to foreign symlinks?  I still like the idea of having it be a general flag - It does not have to be a full immutable if, as Bruno said, that doesn't work for the requirement here.

But I think having the ability to mark files as non-removable is interesting, and having a generic mechanism seems beneficial, rather than one limited to foreign symlinks.
